    "20de17b1-1607-4828-bbd7-bada19a3c33c": {
      "children": [
        "dde54cf6-1e27-4723-9ea1-132d42b89d6b"

      "id": "20de17b1-1607-4828-bbd7-bada19a3c33c",

        "content": {
          "content_type": "text",
          "parts": [
            "INTERLUDE I: Perfect and Pure\n\n\nCopper-gold warmth flooded his chest, then burned.\nPART A: CORLEXI—PERFECT LINES\n\nPrism was all angles pretending to be virtue. Corlexi loved it for that lie.\n\nHe stood on a ribbed gallery high in the half-built Spire of Measures, wind combed thin through the lattice, apprentices scattered below like commas in a sentence that would not end. Chalk lines webbed the floor. Plumb-threads hung perfectly still—not because the air was calm, but because he refused motion.\n\n“Again,” he said.\n\nThey lifted the truss and set it into the mouth of the waiting frame. Blue-silver threaded his fingers and stayed, a constant wire under the skin. He pressed it into the join—not hard, not soft, exactly—until the two faces of steel forgot their seam. The Spire’s hum shifted half a note closer to satisfied.\n\n“Master,” Adren ventured, careful. “We’ve been at it three watches.”\n\n“We are not tired,” Corlexi said, and made the statement feel true the way a line becomes true when enough force is applied. The boy straightened. Everyone did.\n\nA brace complained far below—soft, then quiet, chastened by a glance Corlexi did not bother to send. The city beyond lay sharpened by late glow, every roofline cutting the sky. He loved the certainty of edges. Loved the moment when a bracket’s petty war with gravity ended and the bracket conceded he had always been right. Disaster had a geometry; it could be designed against. If he perfected the forms, the world would remember how to hold itself.\n\nThey shifted the west run. Adren’s boot slipped on chalk and oil. He snatched at air, found nothing, tilted. Meve lunged, caught a sleeve, lost purchase. Corlexi moved a hand-width—no farther—caught Adren’s collar, kept the line of the truss with his other hand as if both tasks were one equation. Blue-silver whispered at his knuckles where they touched steel. The apprentice hung a breath over the drop, feet bicycling emptily.\n\n“Still,” Corlexi said, as if calming a beam. Adren froze. Corlexi set the boy upright without permitting the truss to skew a single finger off true. The metal sang compliance. He released the collar last.\n\n“Thank you, Master,” Adren said, scarce air and shame in it.\n\n“Do not thank me for maintaining form,” Corlexi said. “Thank the form for permitting you to remain inside it.”\n\nThey worked on. The glow that had begun as event sat now like background, like breath. A pleasant pressure gathered in Corlexi’s knuckles; his fingers did not want to fold. He did not require them to. He shaped force through flat hands and let his wrists carry the line. Hands that lacked discipline shook; structures did not. He preferred structures.\n\nMeve squinted along the north run. “A hair over-stiff there. If wind takes a mood, we’ll get chatter.”\n\n“Remove the hair,” Corlexi said, “after we seat this.”\n\nBlue-silver settled into the truss like a clean number. The Spire answered with a long, low approval. Corlexi let himself breathe.\n\nHe imagined a city where every rib and brace and gutter held to this logic. Where bulges in the sky—whatever they were—could find no purchase because there were no irregularities to amplify. Where people lived inside certainty and forgot the taste of fear.\n\nHis thumb would not touch his forefinger. He watched the failure to meet with mild curiosity, as if it belonged to some other man left on his scaffold by mistake. He tried the other hand. Same result. Stiffness; bright, clean pain when he insisted. A ledger line, not a warning.\n\n“Water,” he said at last, magnanimous. “A swallow. Then the west truss.”\n\nRelief moved across the crew like wind over grass. He let it. They drank. They breathed. The blue-silver under his skin did not dim.\n\nPerfection requires sacrifice. He had always been willing to pay.\n\nPART B: MOBEL—CLEANSING FIRE\n\nThe desert at Heattide stripped the polite off things. Mobel liked the honesty.\n\nHis tent was a shadow pinned to hard ground, canvas singing under a sun that refused to age. The woman on the pallet had a wound along the thigh that smelled like rot turned argumentative. Her husband knelt beside her with hope stretched thin between both hands, the way men hold rope when the beam is already failing.\n\nMobel washed his fingers in water he could have drunk and did not. He wiped them dry and worked with what he had: boiled cloth, clean band, a narrow iron warmed in coals until it went the color of admission. Heat has a voice; it speaks of endings. He let it speak through his hand.\n\n“Hold her,” he said.\n\nThe woman screamed once, clean and strong. Flesh bubbled, then flattened. The stink lifted and left something metallic and sharp behind. He walked the wound’s edge with care, burning away anything that argued with health. “Contamination requires fire,” Mobel said, as he said for all, a simple litany to steady hands. “Clean is the law.”\n\nOutside the tent, a knot of watchers held their breath in a single borrowed chest. They had followed him here—quiet women with hard faces; men with scars and eyes that had stopped searching for soft places; two youths too young to be certain and hungry for someone who seemed to be. They liked the clarity he offered. He liked that they liked it. It made the work simpler.\n\nHe bound the wound in boiled cloth. The woman sobbed into the cool and then, exhausted, slept. Her husband reached to kiss Mobel’s hands. Mobel lifted them out of reach. The skin had swollen from the iron—a pressure under the knuckles like water seeking a seam. He flexed and felt the complaint spread along the tendons like a fault line mapping itself. He filed it as inventory. Costs were comfort when counted correctly.\n\nA second couple pushed forward. The man’s forearm was banded with ink that crawled into an old cut. The skin around it went the wrong colors. “Please,” the woman said, throat hoarse. “We walked a reach.”\n\nMobel looked at the arm, then at the ink. “You kept filth in the skin,” he said, not loud. “You chose it.”\n\n“It’s my clan,” the man rasped. “Not filth.”\n\n“Then let your clan heal you,” Mobel said, and stepped aside. The watchers murmured—approval more than anger, relief at a rule applied. The woman begged again, soft, the way people do when their words have no leverage left.\n\nMobel did not compete with the desert. The desert corrected everything eventually.\n\nHe stepped into the sun because he liked the way heat made the ache in his hands feel less like pain and more like law. Wind picked up; the tent answered with a different song, one that had learned the low third note threading the world since the sky had bulged and passed. Mobel ignored it. His note was simpler: clean or not.\n\nHe looked east, where the horizon cut pure across sand, and thought of cities with their compromises. Thought of the way rot hid in corners and called itself neighborly. He rested swollen hands against the tent pole until the ache made a proper accounting.\n\n“Only the clean will stand,” he said. Words moved through the watchers like a heat-front, leaving belief behind in their wake.\n\nThen he went back in to boil more cloth, to pour more water he would not drink, to answer one more body with the fire it deserved.\n\n\nInterlude II: Rumor & Report \nSalee—Everyone’s Pain \nCauldron-Hold called itself a clinic again because someone had wiped the ash off the sign. Salee didn’t argue with the name. Names kept people walking in. \nThey came in bent and left a little taller. That was the work. She took the worst of it. \nA line trailed out past the basins to the alley mouth—old burns that had learned to ache, fresh breaks that hadn’t learned manners, fevers that talked in riddles. She moved from pallet to pallet with a wet cloth and clean thread and the quiet voice that made people remember how to breathe. When her hand rested near a wound, the room tilted. Heat shifted. Pain leaned toward her like metal toward a magnet and then slid, obedient, under her skin. \nThe first man had a rib that wouldn’t let him breathe all the way. She set her palm near the bruise and listened. The tightness gathered like a fist and then unfurled itself into her. He exhaled to the bottom for the first time in a tide. “Bless you,” he said, astonished. She nodded and went to the next. \nBy watch’s end she had a tally of blessings, a basin of thread ends, and two forearms that had learned a new map: copper-brown lines writing themselves with neat malice, curving from palm-heels toward elbow’s bend. She washed them with the same cloth she used on other people and didn’t look long. Looking made the ache louder. \nA woman came in carrying a child who had not decided whether to stay. Salee took the weight, took the small hand, and let the room tilt again. The child’s eyes widened, then softened. The mother went to her knees and held Salee’s skirt like it was rope. \n“You’re taking it,” the mother whispered. \n“I’m borrowing it,” Salee said, which was the same lie she told herself. Pain didn’t return on its own. You had to hand it back, and she never remembered how. \nBetween patients, she checked the ledger. Not numbers; a list of names and short notes in a cramped hand: Marn—breath, Fex—hand, Old Juri—sleep. The list steadied her. It made the ache orderly. \nA boy with glass-shy in his palm flinched from the basin. “It will hurt,” he said, already ashamed. \n“It will,” she agreed. “Then it won’t.” She took his wrist, set her other hand near the glittering specks, and invited the sting to change direction. It came obediently, quick and bright. For a breath she couldn’t feel her own palm at all. When sensation returned, it was thinner, like light through milk. \n“Better?” she asked. \nHe nodded, surprised at his own courage, and left the basin grinning. She added Ktt—shy to the ledger. \nBy late watch, her hands trembled in a fine, irritating buzz. Someone offered her a cup. She smiled and forgot to drink it. People thanked her with bread, with buttons, with the way they stood up straighter. She stacked thanks on the shelf with the thread. The shelf sagged. \nAt the door, a man with a soldier’s old back asked, not unkindly, “What do you keep for yourself?” \nSalee looked at her palms—the lines a little darker now, climbing with diligent intent—and tried to recall the last time her body had complained in her own voice. The memory ducked out of reach like a shy animal. \n“I don’t remember what my pain feels like,” she said, and surprised herself with the truth of it. \nThe man bowed as if that were a sacred answer and left before she could take the weight of his gratitude. \nWhen the bell lied about rest, she turned the sign anyway. The alley grumbled; the city did not lack for injuries. A girl with fever stood already in the doorway, swaying. \nSalee raised her hands. The lines glowed dull and did not ask permission. \n“If I take all the pain,” she told the room, not looking to see who heard, “no one has to suffer.” No one argued. She went back to work. \nEries—Endings Are Natural \nVenn Eries chose a quiet table beneath the temple’s unlit lamp and arranged his pages with care. Ink, straightedge, a neat stack of fools’ comfort. He called it a treatise to make the shaking in his fingers feel like industry. \nOn the Necessity of Endings. \nHe wrote the title again because the first time was untidy. Then a sentence that had been waiting behind his teeth since the Piercing: Continuance without purpose is cruelty. He paused, not for thought, but to measure the breath it took to commit the words to the page. Breath was a unit you could count; grief was not. \nNovices swept ash into orderly lines and avoided his table. The elders did not. They came in a cluster—polite, troubled, already decided. \n“Venn,” said the oldest, whose hands had buried more people than most storms. “You are scaring the mourners.” \n“I am consoling them,” Eries said, and put a period down with exact force. “I am teaching that endings are not failures. They are the mercy of design.” \n“A philosophy of surrender,” another said. \n“A philosophy of kindness,” Eries replied. He looked up and let them see how tired his eyes had grown in so few tides. “Release is a form of love. To force a grip past its honesty is violence.” They flinched at violence—a temple word, not to be used on priests. The oldest set a gentle palm on the page without smearing the ink. “You are dismissed from the hall,” he said, voice good at mercy. “Take your pages with you. Do not bring them back.” \nEjection did not feel like a fall. It felt like someone taking a weight off a beam already bowed. Eries gathered the treatise, left the lamp unlit, and walked into a street that had learned to speak in bells. \nBy the temple steps, three people waited as if they had known exactly when he would be thrown out. A woman with a healer’s hands and the tremor of someone who hadn’t slept. A man with a laborer’s shoulders wearing grief like a wet coat. A boy with ash on his eyelashes and no one’s hand to hold. \n“Are you Venn Eries?” the woman asked. The boy stared at the pages. \n“I am,” he said, surprised to hear his name still fit. \n“We heard you tell a woman to let go,” the man said, wary and hopeful in the same breath. “That she didn’t have to keep her father breathing through the night if there wasn’t any of him left to come back.” \n“She hit me,” Eries said, and found a smile that didn’t belong to cruelty. “Then she slept.” \nThe boy nodded like he understood something adults often hid from him. “Can you teach us,” he asked, “how to do… that? The letting?” \n“I can name it,” Eries said. “I can make it less frightening.” \nHe led them to a table that was not a temple’s. In the corner of a bread-shop that had decided to be a school for a watch, he opened the treatise and read the first paragraph aloud. People turned their heads; a few sat down without asking why. \nAs he spoke, his skin felt a size too large, like a garment you keep wearing for memory’s sake. The vitality leak was not dramatic—no gasp, no glamour—only a steady thinness, like pouring a jar in slow drops that never seemed to end. The woman’s eyes tracked it with the disgust of a practitioner who knew costs and hated to be grateful for them. \n“This will age you,” she said after the reading, blunt as duty. \n“It already has,” Eries said, and lifted his hand to show her the truth: veins a little darker, spots of chill under the skin where warmth didn’t bother staying. “Endings always do.” \nElders came to the shop door and hesitated—authority didn’t like rooms that named its limits. Passersby paused, listened, and found themselves sitting. A man who’d carried his mother’s body in his arms took the chair closest to the treatise and cried without apology. Eries handed him a cloth and kept reading. \nRelease is the kindest gift, he wrote on a fresh page, to make sure the sentence would exist even if the bread-shop burned and the temple forgot him. \nSomeone asked from the back, scared and angry at once: “If everything ends, why build? Why love?” \n“Because endings make meaning,” Eries said, voice steady enough to carry. “Not less. More.” \nHe did not look back at the temple. He didn’t need its lamp. Outside, the city tested its braces and held, for now, at the edge of a proof it was not ready to see. Eries stacked his pages, felt the years add their quiet weight, and accepted the arithmetic. \n“All things end,” he told the room, and the room believed him because he looked the part. “Why \nfight it?”"
          ]

          "text": "{\"name\":\"N01 — Revised Chapters 11–15 (Tracked Changes)\",\"type\":\"document\",\"content\":\"### Chapter 11: Fracture Edge — (Jhace POV)\\n\\nThe span was wrong before they set a hand on it. Hanger bolts whispered their little lies; the riser sang a thin wire above the grid’s hum. Jhace tasted copper so strong it felt like biting a coin.\\n\\n“Sequence,” he said. “Clamp, pre-shape, seat, test.”\\n\\n“Clamp,” Tiffani answered, already moving. Bram took the pry. Chloen took gauges with her mouth set to serious.\\n\\nThey bled the first head and the song did not settle. The low third-note—the one the world had acquired and refused to give back—pushed against Jhace’s bones in a bad cadence.\\n\\n“Hold,” Tiffani called at the second clamp. He did not love that he stopped. He loved that he stopped. The pact held.\\n\\n“Two heads and a finger,” Chloen reported. “Climbing.”\\n\\n“Seat,” Jhace said. He placed the key. His right hand **~~stayed steady~~** **shook a fraction**. He set his weight anyway—\\n\\n—and the world went thin.\\n\\nVision narrowed like looking through a dropped sight. Sound went to drum and wire. The riser under his palm developed a hunger that wasn’t appetite; it was **absence,** as if the metal wanted to be a gap more than it wanted to be itself.\\n\\n“Jhace.” Tiffani’s voice reached him through the wire. “Release.”\\n\\nHe couldn’t trust his fingers. He trusted her. He let go. The key clanged against the hanger and would have fallen if Bram hadn’t caught it one-handed with a curse that sounded like fondness.\\n\\n“Back,” Tiffani said. Bram pulled; Chloen moved; Jhace let himself be the thing moved. He hated that. He kept breathing anyway.\\n\\nThe grid’s hum shifted again—higher, then lower, then **stacked.** A hanger two spans over squealed like a pinched animal.\\n\\n“Pre-shape,” Tiffani said, palms already on the cross-line she’d chalked an hour ago when she’d studied the wall like a problem. The **blue** breathed under her hands. The hanger’s squeal dropped to whine.\\n\\n“Seat on my call,” she said.\\n\\nHe heard the authority and didn’t fight it. She rode the load a beat, then, “Now.”\\n\\nHe set the key and pulled—controlled, not brave. The pin bit. The song smoothed into something the body could live with.\\n\\n“Two heads,” Chloen said. “Stable. Stable.” She didn’t try for a third.\\n\\nJhace leaned against the rib, **~~furious~~** **breathing,** the copper taste gone to iron. The low third-note still pressed. His sight came back slow, like opening his hand after it cramped.\\n\\nBram’s eyes had the patient anger of an old man outliving his pride. “Say it.”\\n\\n“Vein’s at **1.2**,” Jhace said, honesty dragging over rock. “Near-Hollow pull for a breath. Vision narrowed. **Fog** at the edges.”\\n\\nTiffani’s jaw worked once and then steadied. She didn’t touch him. She set a clamp by his hip and made that the touch. “We don’t do that again,” she said. Not scold. Decision.\\n\\nHe wanted to argue. He wanted to be the wheel-hand forever. He wanted to be alive at the end of the watch. He said, “Fine.”\\n\\nThey moved along the span and made the rest true. The work behaved because they had. **~~It felt like a loss.~~** **It felt like something heavier than pride being set down without breaking.**\\n\\nAt the end of the run, the low third-note picked a new rhythm. It tugged not just at metal—at him. A **gray** pull, distant, like being leaned on by a wall you couldn’t see.\\n\\n“Feel that?” he asked, because lying about sensation made you stupid.\\n\\nTiffani nodded once. “I feel **tug**. I don’t know its math.”\\n\\n“That makes two of us,” Bram said, and spat in a way that did not help the numbers.\\n\\nThey packed tools. Jhace’s right hand tremored in a small neat line that would not take instruction. He didn’t hide it. The pact had rules.\\n\\nTiffani walked beside him without trying to make anything lighter. That helped more than anything else could have.\\n\\n**<!--Beats: Multi-fail/near-fade, Tiffani’s reciprocated save, Bram witness; Costs: Near-Hollow scar sensation (unnamed), Vein 1.2; Tease: gray tug distant; Voice: short, tactile; one dynamics change: reciprocity (she commands; he trusts).-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 12: Drift Align — (Tiffani POV)\\n\\nMorning put a thin light on the clamps and made their shadows precise. Tiffani tested her hands—stiffness at seventy percent by her internal scale; tremor latent if she pushed. Manageable if she respected it.\\n\\nJhace stood at the bench with his sleeves rolled and his right hand honest about its limitations. He did not look away when she looked. That was new.\\n\\n“I want to see the scar,” she said.\\n\\nHe made a face at the word **scar** like it had presumptions. He set his forearm on the table anyway and turned the wrist. Vein showed under the skin—a darker thread that had not been there, a **line 1.2** long by finger measure from the wrist-bone toward the thumb base. **~~Ugly~~** **Unforgiving.**\\n\\nShe set two fingers near it and did not touch. “It is not going backward.”\\n\\n“I know,” he said. Also new.\\n\\n“It will advance if you choose spectacle.”\\n\\n“I know that, too.”\\n\\nShe let the ledger in her voice soften. “I would like you to live.”\\n\\nHe huffed something that wasn’t laughter and wasn’t not. “I would like that, too.”\\n\\nShe turned her hands, palms up, offered data. “Stiffness seventy percent. Fine control reduced. I can buy you holds if I aim at the cross-lines and **spend** carefully.”\\n\\nHe looked at her hands like the tools they were and not like something he wasn’t allowed to use. “I accept the holds.”\\n\\nThe acceptance moved something large inside her—**not romance;** **alignment.** She breathed into the new geometry of it.\\n\\nShe felt the moment arrive before she knew its name. Her mouth said it. “I want to kiss you now.”\\n\\nHe blinked like a man who’d been offered a wheel when he expected a pry. “You sure?”\\n\\n“Yes,” she said, and found that the word did not fracture her. It made her clearer. “Because yesterday I thought you would break in front of me, and it felt like someone cutting a brace I was tied to. Because you listened when I said release. Because you say **no** to crowds with me. Because I am precise and this is true.”\\n\\n“Okay,” he said, simple as a seated pin.\\n\\nShe stepped in and set her mouth to his—careful, as if aligning glass edges. He tasted like metal and **~~anger~~** **relief** and the tea Bram pretended he didn’t brew strong. His right hand didn’t lift. His left did, to the table’s edge. He kissed like a man learning a new tool without pretending he already knew it.\\n\\nWhen she drew back, the room had not fallen. The world had not punished accuracy.\\n\\n“I keep this,” she said, and the corners of his mouth did a small honest thing.\\n\\n“Keep it,” he agreed.\\n\\n**// SLOT B — Post-reveal cost talk (variant)**\\n\\nShe lifted his hand by the wrist and set it back down. “We add two rules for me,” she said. “If the stiffness passes eighty, I do not pre-shape. If my tremor shows in the ledger lines, I call stop, and you accept it.”\\n\\nHe weighed that with his jaw. “And for me: if the **vein** shows at **1.4**, I step off wheels and stay off.”\\n\\n“Say **1.3**,” she said. “We bias safe.”\\n\\nHe almost argued. He didn’t. “1.3,” he said, and the numbers made something in her unclench that had not unclenched since the horizon bowed.\\n\\nThey stood in the quiet they’d made and let it hold.\\n\\n**<!--Beats: Scar reveal; Marisse echo implicit in precision ethic; Kiss (her init); Dynamics: reciprocity and pact refinement; Slot B cost talk inserted; Costs: Stiffness 70%, Jhace vein 1.2; Voice: geometric, balanced.-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 13: Morning-Of — (Jhace POV)\\n\\nThe day began with tools laid in a neat row and the city pretending to be reasonable. Jhace didn’t trust that. He built plans like braces: meant to move load where it would damage least.\\n\\n“Sequence,” he said over the chalk map. “Site A, then B if the world allows moods.”\\n\\n“Pre-shape here,” Tiffani said, tapping a cross-line. “We buy the turn.”\\n\\n“Logged,” Chloen said, and her handwriting had gotten more confident in the way only competence earns.\\n\\nThey ran the morning like a clean machine. Jhace did not take the wheel where he once would have. He pointed. Bram pulled. Tiffani held—smart, not heavy. Chloen called numbers and corrected a vendor who tried to hang a basket on a hanger with a stare that deserved a bracer of its own.\\n\\nRumor walked the streets in paper shoes. Pamphlets muttered **“endings west”** in woodcut letters that thought themselves brave. Jhace didn’t read them. He read metal.\\n\\nBy midlight they’d done what could be done and refused what needed refusing. Vein held at **1.2**. Tremor threaded everything and did not ruin it. That was the bar today.\\n\\nPeople watched. Less a crowd, more a weather. Jhace felt eyes like heat.\\n\\nBram handed him a copper bracer he’d cut down and refit. “Wear this,” Bram said. “It doesn’t make you immortal. It makes you honest.”\\n\\nJhace buckled it and felt better and worse. “You don’t have to be my father,” he said, not cruel.\\n\\n“I’m not,” Bram said. “I’m your crew.”\\n\\nJhace nodded once. He didn’t deserve that and also he did.\\n\\n**// SLOT C — End fear hand-hold**\\n\\nThey climbed a flight to cross to the last rib. Tiffani’s step faltered half a count, not from weakness, from thinking too many moves ahead. He felt it the way you feel a hanger sing a hair high.\\n\\nHe didn’t reach for her hand like a boy. He set his palm up between them like offering a tool.\\n\\nShe placed her hand there and matched his pace. “One person,” Chloen said from behind, teasing and not, and they didn’t correct her because the words weren’t wrong.\\n\\nThey reached the rib as a unit. The day would try to take that from them. It would fail.\\n\\n**<!--Beats: Prep sync; rumor; Chloen’s watch line; Dynamics: public acknowledgment, Bram bracer handoff; Slot C: fear hand-hold; Costs: vein stable at 1.2; Tease: “endings west.”-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 14: Weight Test — (Tiffani POV)\\n\\nThe site waited with its patient wrongness. Hangers leaned a hair. The wall had learned bad posture from people who loved it too hard.\\n\\nTiffani placed her palms and felt the map inside the material. **Surface tension** carried into structure. Flow made shape. She could hold this if she paid correctly.\\n\\n“Clamp,” Jhace said.\\n\\n“Clamp,” she echoed, and the echo felt like partnership rather than repetition.\\n\\nThey bled the first head. The hum dropped. The crowd—smaller than yesterday—settled into watching without asking for theater.\\n\\nHalfway through the sequence, a hanger at the far left sang sharp. Jhace moved—then didn’t, because he’d learned the new courage. He pointed. Bram took wheel. Tiffani deepened the hold at the cross and felt her fine control fray at the edges like a string pulled too long.\\n\\n“Stop,” Jhace said, and she wanted to argue because she could still shape it, but the pact demanded obedience both ways. She stepped off the hold, fingers shaking in the small controlled way that meant she had spent correctly.\\n\\nThey reset and finished. The wall forgave them for being human.\\n\\nThe declaration arrived as a structural necessity. She could not carry the next span without saying the thing that aligned the load.\\n\\n“I need your hand,” she said to Jhace, and took it without waiting for approval, because the approval had been earned a dozen times this week.\\n\\nThe crowd made its little sound. She ignored it. “I love you,” she said, and the words arranged the rest of her into true. Not a performance. A load path.\\n\\nHe didn’t make it an echo. He made it a brace. “We’ll hold,” he said. The promise shaped itself like a ring on a hanger: not pretty; absolutely functional.\\n\\nChloen’s face went soft in the way of people who’ve found home in a sentence they weren’t in. Bram’s mouth twitched and then didn’t, because a man is allowed his private graces.\\n\\nThey finished the site with hands that were fifty percent reliable and a trust that was absolute. The city didn’t clap. It didn’t need to.\\n\\n**<!--Beats: Trust absolute; reinforce under fail; declaration pre-stakes (“Love you”); Dynamics: Tiffani–Jhace reliance/commit; Costs: hands 50%; tremor baseline; Tease: crowd murmurs of “fires.” Voice: geometric clarity.-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 15: Set True — (Jhace POV)\\n\\nAfternoon put a hard light on Rib Three and made every flaw look like confession. The public phases had been promised by a man in boots who did not carry tools. They would do the work anyway.\\n\\n“Sequence,” Jhace said, because the word made the air less stupid.\\n\\nThey began. Tiffani held at the cross with a control that had cost her all day; Bram took wheels with the patience of a floodplain; Chloen made gauge numbers into commands the way good apprentices do when they grow teeth.\\n\\nThe first phase stood. The second wavered, thought about failure, and remembered manners.\\n\\nOn the third, a hanger pin on the east face decided to be honest about its limits. It went with a clean **bang** and the wheel lurched.\\n\\nJhace didn’t think. He moved. Left hand to wheel, right to pry, body between metal and people. The tremor turned his hand into a bad instrument; he used it anyway and compensated with stance.\\n\\nThe wheel tried to break his wrist. Bram’s arm appeared under his like a brace you hadn’t budgeted for and were grateful to find. Tiffani’s voice cut under the noise: “Release.” He did, because he had learned how to survive.\\n\\nThe wheel spun; the hanger seated ugly and then true. The wall groaned and then decided to keep being a wall.\\n\\nJhace staggered two steps backward. The ground did that tilt that belonged to him, not the world. He went to a knee he didn’t entirely trust and felt the **vein** pull like something being written deeper.\\n\\n“Numbers,” he said through a mouth that didn’t want to be used.\\n\\n“Three heads,” Chloen said. “Stable. Stable.”\\n\\nHe got to his feet. Pride was a tool; you used it when it served the job. “Again.”\\n\\nThey set the last phase. The crowd breathed, the way crowds do when they’ve been reminded breath is not guaranteed.\\n\\nAfter, on the roof—because roofs had been where truths happen since the first person looked down and decided to try again—they stood in the wind and let their bones cool.\\n\\nTiffani lifted her hand, palm up. He set his palm to it, the way he had when he pulled her out of wrongness the first time. **~~He kissed her mouth.~~** **He kissed her palm,** a mirror and a vow.\\n\\n“You’re at **3.0**,” she said. Not accusation. Record.\\n\\n“Permanent,” he said. Not bravado. Fact.\\n\\n“We plan around it,” she said. “Costs don’t make us holy. They make us careful.”\\n\\n“Careful keeps people alive,” Bram put in from the roof’s edge. He wasn’t pretending not to listen. He was pretending to give them privacy by looking at the horizon the way men pretend not to look at a sunset.\\n\\nThe city below had learned some of its weight and forgotten some of its vanity. Posters at the corner ribs muttered **“lines snap north.”** The wind made a noise like a brace deciding to stay.\\n\\n**// SLOT A — End Debrief (what now)**\\n\\nThey sat with backs to the proof rib. Chloen wrapped her burned hand with new gauze because she’d learned to do it herself.\\n\\n“Next,” Jhace said, once his breath agreed to be useful.\\n\\n“Scale work,” Tiffani said. “Private holds. Crew training. No performances. We publish a field sheet that says **no** in three polite ways and one impolite way.”\\n\\nBram grunted. “Make the impolite one large.”\\n\\n“Costs logged,” Chloen said, writing. “Vein three point zero. Permanent. Hands at fifty. Tremor baseline.” She looked up, dared. “And four people who don’t work alone anymore.”\\n\\nJhace let that sit. It didn’t make him itch. It made him feel like a pin seated under a load that finally admitted where it lived.\\n\\nHe looked at Tiffani’s palm and kissed it again, smaller. “What now,” he said, and for the first time in a long time, the answer wasn’t **alone**.\\n\\n**<!--Beats: Public phases; collapse/catch; rooftop; palm kiss (Ch3 mirror); Group: load unity; Costs: vein 3.0cm permanent; Tease: posters; Slot A debrief plans “what now.” Voice: short, tactile.-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Phase 3 Mini Audit (Ch11–Ch15)\\n\\n| Ch | Beats Hit | Dynamics (1/scene) | Slots Used | Costs/Tease | Notes |\\n|----|-----------|---------------------|------------|-------------|------|\\n| 11 | Multi-fail; fade; pull-back | Jhace–Tiffani reciprocity (she commands; he trusts) | — | Vein **1.2**; Near-Hollow **fog**; **gray tug** tease | Crisis controlled by pact; Bram witness |\\n| 12 | Scar reveal; kiss (her init) | Tiffani–Jhace scar mirror → commitment | **Slot B (cost talk variant)** | Stiffness **70%**; vein **1.2** | Pact refined with numeric thresholds (1.3 bias) |\\n| 13 | Prep sync; rumor; watch | Jhace–Tiffani public acknowledgment; Bram bracer | **Slot C (fear hand-hold)** | Vein **1.2** stable | Rumor: **“endings west”** pamphlets |\\n| 14 | Weight test; reinforce; declare | Tiffani–Jhace rely/commit (“Love you”) | — | Hands **50%**; tremor baseline | Declaration pre-stakes, not post |\\n| 15 | Public phases; rooftop | Jhace–Tiffani mirror (palm kiss); group unity | **Slot A (what now debrief)** | Vein **3.0** permanent; posters **“lines snap north”** | Ends with motion: scale plan; no performances |\"}"

For clever.\" He flexed \nhis hand, feeling the tremor thread through the movement. \"If I give them performance, \nthe vein moves past 0.5 and we lose margin.\"\n\nShe aligned herself with him, shoulder near shoulder. \"Then we don't perform,\" \nshe said. \"We work. They can watch work or they can leave.\"\n\nHe nodded once. The pact held. They climbed.\n```\n\n**Why**: Gives Jhace **vulnerability moment before crowd test**, making the public demonstration of restraint more meaningful. Currently, the crowd scene shows pact working but not Jhace's internal negotiation.\n\n**Priority**: Medium. Chapter works without it, but Slot C in audit table suggests this was intended.\n\n***\n\n## **CHAPTER 8: CITY GRAMMAR** ✅ **MASTERFUL**\n\n### **What Works**\n\n✅ **Opening**: \"They called it a demonstration. It was a crowd with opinions and a set of gates that had been stuck since before some of the opinions learned to speak.\" — **Dry wit** (character voice + situation irony).\n\n✅ **Jhace to crowd**: \"If you want performance, buy a song. If you want the gate to live, wait.\" — **Perfect**. Authority through refusal.\n\n✅ **Cost escalation critical**: Vein at 0.8 (jumped from 0.5), \"Hallucination light\" (new symptom), nausea visible. **Stakes now severe**.\n\n✅ **Public cost accounting**: Jhace says costs **to the work**, but crowd hears none—**correct balance** (pact is between crew, not performance).\n\n✅ **Slot A (End Debrief)** deployed perfectly:\n- Cost accounting explicit\n- Scale-down decision (\"We scale down public work\")\n- \"Say it with me\" / \"No\" — **Unity through refusal**\n\n✅ **Bram's line**: \"Gross holds is a phrase I never needed.\" / \"I meant large amplitude.\" — **Character-consistent humor** (breaks tension without undermining stakes).\n\n### **Micro-Fix: None**\n\nThis chapter is **10/10**. Touch nothing.\n\n***\n\n## **CHAPTER 9: FIELD MANUAL** ✅ **STRONG**\n\n### **What Works**\n\n✅ **Opening**: \"The hall didn't care about geometry. People arranged themselves by grievance and hope; both refused symmetry.\" — **Tiffani voice** (geometric observation of chaos).\n\n✅ **Tiffani to room**: \"We are not here to sort your politics. We are here to explain what keeps walls from behaving like suggestions.\" — **Authority through precision**.\n\n✅ **Cost transparency**: \"His vein is at 0.8 and will not go backward. My hands stiffen and tremor if I overreach.\" — **Public honesty** (teaches cost-accounting to city).\n\n✅ **Jhace's answer**: \"Do you get scared?\" / \"Yes. If I don't, I'm not paying attention.\" — **Vulnerability as competence**.\n\n✅ **\"So you're together\" question**: Room probes romantic angle, Tiffani deflects with \"partners in the work,\" leaves \"other words unspent.\" **Perfect restraint**.\n\n✅ **Slot A (short debrief)**: \"Public claim\" / \"No\" with multiple meanings — **Economical, earned**.\n\n### **Micro-Fix #1: Slot A Expansion**\n\n**Current Slot A**: Only 2 lines. Feels **slightly abrupt** after the weight of the hall scene.\n\n**Suggested expansion** (add 3-4 sentences):\n\n```\nThey closed the door behind the last hand and leaned, because people are a load.\n\n\"Public claim,\" Tiffani said.\n\nJhace's mouth didn't move, but his eyes did something that meant no and also \nmeant not yet and also meant I heard you. \"No,\" he said again, quieter. It had \nother meanings now—refusal of performance, refusal of premature naming, agreement \nthat the work came first and the rest would follow when it earned its place.\n\nShe heard them all and filed them under Future.\n```\n\n**Why**: Current version **works** but feels compressed. The added sentences let readers **feel Jhace's negotiation** without stating it explicitly.\n\n**Priority**: Low-medium. Current version functional.\n\n***\n\n## **CHAPTER 10: UNDER LOAD** ✅ **EXCELLENT**\n\n### **What Works**\n\n✅ **Opening**: \"Planning wanted to be clean. The city wanted to be messy. They met in the yard and negotiated.\" — **Perfect metaphor** (work = negotiation between ideal and real).\n\n✅ **Jhace to Chloen**: \"You'll get it honest. Right follows.\" — **Teaching philosophy** (honesty before accuracy).\n\n✅ **Slot C (Vulnerability Confession)** — **PERFECT DEPLOYMENT**:\n- \"I can't carry all of this.\" — **First-person vulnerability** (Jhace never uses \"I\" about limits)\n- \"I don't know how to not be the person who takes the wheel when it needs taking.\" — **Core wound** (identity = burden-carrier)\n- Tiffani: \"Then be the person who calls the sequence. It's the same courage with a different grip.\" — **Reframes role** without diminishing him\n- \"Hold me to it.\" / \"I will\" — **Pact evolution** (not just operational, personal)\n\n✅ **Ending intimacy**: \"Tiffani brushed his sleeve with the back of her hand—accident not accident; a touch that said the thing neither of them would name yet.\" — **Perfect restraint**. Not romantic escalation—acknowledgment.\n\n✅ **Cost tracking**: \"Tremor constant\" (now baseline, not symptom), refusal earns wall survival (**consequences shown**).\n\n### **Micro-Fix #1: Slot C Positioning**\n\n**Current**: Slot C happens \"in the shadow of a proof rib\" with crowd nearby.\n\n**Observation**: The intimacy of Jhace's confession (\"I can't carry all of this\") feels **slightly exposed** with crowd present, even if they can't hear.\n\n**Suggested adjustment**: Add one sentence establishing **privacy**:\n\n```\nThey paused in the shadow of a proof rib. The crowd swelled a pace ahead and \nthen held a respectful line because they'd been taught yesterday. Behind the \nrib, the sound of the crowd dulled to sea-noise.\n\nJhace said, without looking at her, \"I can't carry all of this.\"\n```\n\n**Why**: The added \"Behind the rib, sound dulled\" establishes that this moment is **private**, making Jhace's vulnerability feel safer (he wouldn't confess limitation where crowd could hear).\n\n**Priority**: Low. Current version works, but spatial clarity helps.\n\n***\n\n## **PHASE 2 MINI AUDIT RESPONSE**\n\nYour self-audit is **accurate**:\n\n| Ch | Beats Hit | Dynamics (1/scene) | Slots Used | Costs/Tease | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| 6 | Teaching sync | Tiffani-Jhace warmth; Tiffani-Chloen share | — | Tiffani stiffness/tremor | Rhythm established |\n| 7 | 2-site + crowd | Jhace-Tiffani trust; Jhace-Chloen inclusion | Slot C (variant) | Vein 0.5; pact public | Market scene strong |\n| 8 | Public demo; nausea | Jhace-Tiffani care-conflict; Bram caution | Slot A (debrief) | Vein 0.8; hallucination | \"No performance\" rule |\n| 9 | Faction wedge | Tiffani-Jhace unity; Tiffani-Bram reliance | Slot A (short) | Political cost | Respects denial |\n| 10 | Work choice; brush | Jhace-Tiffani vulnerability; Chloen honesty | Slot C (vulnerability) | Tremor constant | Refusal earns survival |\n\n**Observations**:\n- ✅ **One relational beat per scene** (never stacks)\n- ✅ **Slot deployment correct** (Ch7 Slot C needs fuller deployment, Ch8 Slot A perfect, Ch9 Slot A could expand, Ch10 Slot C perfect)\n- ✅ **Cost escalation visible**: 0.5 → 0.8 → constant, hallucinations debut\n- ✅ **Partnership Phase complete**: Public pact demonstrated (Ch7-8), vulnerability shared (Ch10)\n\n***\n\n## **COST PROGRESSION AUDIT (CH6-10)**\n\n| Chapter | Jhace Vein | Jhace Symptoms | Tiffani Hands | Progression |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| **Ch6** | Not stated | Tremor present | Stiffness/tremor incipient | ✅ Mild |\n| **Ch7** | 0.5cm | Tremor constant | Fine control clean | ✅ Escalates |\n| **Ch8** | 0.8cm | Hallucination light, nausea, vision narrows | Stiffness 70%, tremor under fine tasks | ✅ **Critical jump** |\n| **Ch9** | 0.8cm (stated in hall) | Not shown in scene | Not shown | ✅ Held (public accounting) |\n| **Ch10** | Not stated | Tremor constant (baseline) | Ache mentioned | ✅ Normalized |\n\n**Analysis**: Cost escalation is **visible and escalating correctly**.           "text": "{\"name\":\"N01 — Revised Chapters 6–10 (Tracked Changes)\",\"type\":\"document\",\"content\":\"### Chapter 6: Teaching Rhythm — (Tiffani POV)\\n\\nThe forge did not love straight lines. It loved heat gradients, human error, and the way a good plan softened at the edges under load. Tiffani set the angle-cage on the bench anyway and drew the lattice over the day’s first plate.\\n\\n“Call,” Jhace said from the clamps. He was already arranging the torque keys by cruelty.\\n\\n“Sequence,” she answered. “Clamp, **~~push~~** **pre-shape,** seat, test.”\\n\\n“Clamp,” he echoed. The word fit his hands.\\n\\nChloen hovered, a careful radius from danger and an incautious radius from learning. “Where do you want me?”\\n\\n“Sight for change,” Tiffani said, and pointed. “Here. Eyes on the far edge for cup. You don’t flinch. You report.”\\n\\nChloen’s chin came up like a small flag. “Yes.”\\n\\nTiffani laid her palms on the plate. Not pressure—**not named.** Attention. The chalk lines remembered their purpose. A faint **blue** breathed along the grid. She guided at the cross—the plate’s appetite recognized the invitation.\\n\\n“Hold,” Jhace said, reading her hands like marks on a riser. She kept the touch and let the clamp take a share. The plate settled into something like agreement.\\n\\nBram sorted rivets by size without looking down. He had a way of being background that made everyone else braver. “Remind me why we don’t just weld sense in and go home.”\\n\\n“Because geometry fails honest under live load,” she said. “Better to build for the way people pull.”\\n\\nJhace grunted what might be respect. **~~Or indigestion.~~** **It landed closer to respect.** **<!--Dynamics: Tiffani–Jhace warmth via names/competence; small mirror of language rather than praise-->**\\n\\nThey ran two more plates and traded lead without announcing it. Jhace’s instincts placed clamps where her lattice predicted need. Her lattice pre-shaped where his appetite would otherwise bite later. When Chloen’s voice stuttered, Tiffani glanced, saw the flush of embarrassment, and split the observation in half for her: “First, you report the change you see. Then you say what you think it is.”\\n\\n“I saw cup starting at the far right,” Chloen said. “Small.”\\n\\n“Good,” Tiffani said. “Name the force.”\\n\\n“Uneven pull,” Chloen tried. “Clamp’s biting a hair too close to the line.”\\n\\nJhace shifted the clamp a finger without being asked. The plate sighed. “Better,” he said, and didn’t pretend it had been his idea first.\\n\\nBy middle tide, the rhythm took them—call, hold, release; clamp set, breath gone, breath returned. Tiffani kept count out loud because numbers made air solid for some people. For her, it was the way chords made a song hold together. **~~The forge hated straight lines.~~** **The forge hated straight lines and loved a cadence it could trust.**\\n\\n“Wholeness,” Jhace said once, not to the room, to her. The word carried the exact weight of a bracket seated square. \\n\\nShe met his look and did not drop it. “Wholeness,” she returned, and something in the air accepted the naming.\\n\\nBy last pass, stiffness set into her fingers like a truth written fine. She peeled her palms off the final plate and flexed them once, carefully. Tremor threatened the edges of her control and she caged it with breath.\\n\\nChloen caught it, because of course she did. “You okay?”\\n\\n“I’m precise,” Tiffani said. It was both answer and ward.\\n\\nJhace slid the last clamp free and did not comment. But when she reached for the ledger, he nudged it closer so she did not have to extend. Small kindness. Precise in its own way.\\n\\n**<!--Costs: Tiffani stiffness/tremor incipient; keep Soulpulse unnamed; Dynamics: warmth via \\\"Wholeness\\\" exchange; Chloen authorship share via guided reporting-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 7: Parallel Lines — (Jhace POV)\\n\\nWorksites lied on paper; in steel they told the truth. The first site of the morning sang cooperative. The second had a crowd.\\n\\n“Two checks,” Bram said, scanning faces. “One for metal. One for people.”\\n\\n“People are a load,” Jhace agreed. “They don’t think they are.”\\n\\nThe risers here ran along a low market wall. Vendors had stacked their lives against it—baskets, hooks, the day’s courage. When the hum went wrong, people didn’t stop buying fish. They stared at men with tools and expected rescue to be quiet.\\n\\n“Sequence,” Jhace said, louder. “Clamp, pre-shape, seat, test.”\\n\\n“Clamp,” Tiffani returned from the far hanger, already setting one exactly where he would have. Chloen had the gauge window and a face trying not to make too much of the responsibility.\\n\\nThey bled the first head. The hum dropped. The crowd relaxed a fraction. Relief made people stupid. A man leaned on a rail he shouldn’t. Jhace’s jaw tightened.\\n\\n“Sir,” he said, using the word like a clamp. “Back from the rail. That’s not a suggestion.”\\n\\nThe man squinted as if distance could grow him a backbone. “You lot work for the Crown?”\\n\\n“We work for the metal,” Bram said. “The Crown benefits when it behaves.”\\n\\nThe man’s mouth did something unhelpful and then moved. Jhace put his body where argument wanted to happen and made the argument choose a different place. He set a hand light on the rail and felt the wrongness ripple under his palm.\\n\\n“Hold,” Tiffani called. He froze, lifted, and the crowd saw a man built to refuse stop mid-motion because someone else called the word. They saw the pact function. It changed the air.\\n\\nChloen’s voice came steady. “Two heads. Stable. But the far hanger sings high.”\\n\\nJhace moved without rush. “Seat.” He set the key. “On my pull.”\\n\\n“On your pull,” Bram said.\\n\\nThey took the hanger two teeth. The song smoothed. The market continued pretending nothing was wrong. A child craned for a better view and her mother pulled her back by the hood.\\n\\nThe third note in the world’s song—low, pulsed—nudged Jhace’s bones like a man elbowing through a crowd. It had been living there since the bulge at the horizon; he’d learned to ignore it the way you ignore a bad neighbor.\\n\\n“Vein’s at **0.5**,” he said flatly to Tiffani because they counted costs aloud now. “Tremor’s the same.”\\n\\n“Logged,” she said. “My fine control is clean.”\\n\\nThey were an engine with four parts; it ran. Until the crowd decided to add a fifth.\\n\\nA young man climbed the market wall for a look. His heel knocked a coil of wire down toward the sump run. Chloen flinched toward it. Jhace barked, “No,” and she stopped with her foot over the catwalk gap.\\n\\nThe wire caught on a hanger bolt and held. The crowd made the sound crowds make when something might become spectacle.\\n\\n“Slot,” Bram said under his breath. “We’re not going to win a fight with gravity by consensus.”\\n\\nJhace did not like the word fear. It lived under other names in him: load, span, brace failure. He looked at Tiffani. He didn’t need her lattice for this; he needed what she kept under it. “We’re going to be watched,” he said, which meant: you’re going to feel every eye.\\n\\nShe set her palms on the hanger the way she set them on plates. The **blue** that had no name made the chalk marks he had not made sing like a possibility. She didn’t hold more; she held smarter. He saw the child watching, and the child’s mother watching the child, and the young man watching himself in the reflection of the market window.\\n\\n“Look at me,” Tiffani said to the young man. He did, because command disguised as geometry still commands. “You are adding load to a span that was not meant to carry it. If you want to be part of the repair, climb down and hold your mother’s hand.”\\n\\nThe crowd laughed the way crowds do when they are given a role. The young man flushed and obeyed. A woman near the fish baskets nodded once to herself like a ledger had been balanced.\\n\\n“Seat,” Jhace said softly. “On the cross-line.”\\n\\nThey finished clean. When the hum settled into throat-sung true, the market clapped once—awkward, sincere. Jhace didn’t bow. He did not dislike applause. He distrusted what it bought.\\n\\nOn the walk away, Chloen matched his stride. “When can I call a hold?”\\n\\n“When you’ve seen me ignore one,” he said, honest and not kind.\\n\\nShe nodded like he’d handed her a sharper tool. “I’ll watch.”\\n\\n**<!--Montage trimmed; Site 2 replaced with Slot C variant: fear pre-crowd + public demonstration of pact; Dynamics: Jhace–Tiffani anticipation/trust; Jhace–Chloen inclusion demand; Costs: vein 0.5 logged-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 8: City Grammar — (Jhace POV)\\n\\nThey called it a demonstration. It was a crowd with opinions and a set of gates that had been stuck since before some of the opinions learned to speak.\\n\\nBram hated speeches; he pushed Jhace toward the front like a man nudging a reluctant ox into harness. “You say the fewest words,” Bram said. “That makes people think you’re wise.”\\n\\n“I’m not,” Jhace said.\\n\\n“Exactly.”\\n\\nThey stood before the yard gate that had embarrassed three crews and a pamphlet writer. A handful of city men had clambered up on crates to pretend leadership. The pamphlet writer had better boots than the men with tools.\\n\\n“Show them,” Tiffani said under breath, **~~and it sounded like a plea~~** **and it sounded like faith.**\\n\\n“Sequence,” Jhace said to the work, ignoring the crowd. “Clamp, pre-shape, seat, test.”\\n\\nThe first clamp set clean. The second fought. The wheel wanted to pretend vows again. Jhace felt vomit threaten at the edge of his throat when he leaned—**not fear;** a body pushing back against a world that had pushed too long.\\n\\n“Stop,” Tiffani said, a fraction before his vision narrowed. “Release.”\\n\\nHe did. He stepped back and the ground did a small smart tilt that wasn’t the world—just him. “Logged,” he said when he could use his voice properly. “Vein’s at **0.8**. Hallucination light.” He forced the honesty past the pride because the pact demanded it. The crowd heard none of that, but the four of them did, and the work did, and that was the point.\\n\\nBram shifted to the wheel without flourish. Tiffani set her palms to the hanger with a control that cost her. Chloen stood at the gauge with her mouth a flat line of determination.\\n\\nThey worked. Clamp where the lattice said. Pry where the old metal would accept leverage. The wheel moved and cursed and moved again.\\n\\nSomewhere between second and third pull, someone in the crowd shouted, “Faster!” as if speed were a virtue in this physics.\\n\\nJhace turned his head enough to put the voice in his periphery. “If you want performance, buy a song,” he said. “If you want the gate to live, wait.”\\n\\nLaughter. A little. Enough to buy room.\\n\\nThey seated the last stubborn tooth. The gate’s song shifted from whine to hum. The demonstration applauded because people like endings. Jhace felt none of the joy the clapping pretended at. The low third-note in the world’s song pressed his bones until his jaw clicked.\\n\\nHe held his face straight. Even straight, the nausea crawled up. He swallowed twice. The crowd blurred at the edges.\\n\\n“Back,” Tiffani said, not loud, absolutely heard. He stepped away from the front of the stage they hadn’t built and sat like a man who had chosen to sit. He did not vomit. His pride was not the point. The work was the point. Pride guarded the point when it wasn’t busy ruining it.\\n\\nA pamphlet man stepped close with a mouth full of someone else’s sentences. “This shows,” he began, “that with **coordination** between Crown and—”\\n\\nBram cut him in half with a look. “This shows a gate opens when you stop asking it to be a parade.”\\n\\n“Debrief,” Tiffani said once the tools were back in their homes.\\n\\n“Later,” Jhace said.\\n\\n“Now,” she returned. The pact included debriefs. He hated that. He loved that. **<!--Dynamics: conflict with care; Bram caution pride present-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n**// SLOT A — End Debrief (scale talk, cost accounting, trust under pushback)**\\n\\nThey stole the shade of a brace two streets off the yard. The sound of the crowd dulled to a manageable ignorance. Jhace set his back to the wall and let the nausea finish leaving like a tenant who needed to prove a point on the way out.\\n\\n“Say it,” Tiffani prompted, ledger-true.\\n\\n“Vein at **0.8**,” he said. “Vision narrowed. Nausea. No blackout.”\\n\\nShe flexed her fingers, a slow controlled catalog. “Stiffness seventy percent. Tremor present under fine tasks. Clean control available for gross holds.”\\n\\nBram snorted soft. “Gross holds is a phrase I never needed.”\\n\\nTiffani’s mouth almost smiled. “I meant large amplitude.”\\n\\n“Say large. People stop listening when you stack syllables for fun,” Bram advised.\\n\\nChloen’s eyes stayed on Jhace. “You didn’t hide.”\\n\\n“Can’t fix what we don’t say,” he said. “Can’t trust what we don’t show.”\\n\\nTiffani tipped her head, considering him the way she considered a problem that mattered. “We scale down public work,” she said. “Private holds, controlled sites. No more performances.”\\n\\n“Crowds don’t ask,” Bram said.\\n\\n“They don’t need to,” Jhace said. “We say no.” He met Tiffani’s eyes. “Say it with me.”\\n\\n“No,” she said, **even.** The small unity cost them nothing and bought them much.\\n\\nThey stood. The city still wanted a parade. They gave it a repaired gate instead and called that enough.\\n\\n**<!--Slot A deployed: scale debrief; Dynamics: Jhace–Tiffani trust under pushback; Bram caution pride; Chloen witnesses cost honesty; Costs logged explicitly; Tease continues: low third-note pressure felt-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 9: Field Manual — (Tiffani POV)\\n\\nThe hall didn’t care about geometry. People arranged themselves by grievance and hope; both refused symmetry. Tiffani stood beside Jhace at the front table and refused asymmetry on principle.\\n\\nThe faction man with paper hands spoke for the first block. His words had angles but no load path. The room listened out of habit.\\n\\nWhen he paused to breathe, Tiffani stepped into the gap. “We are not here to sort your politics. We are here to explain what keeps walls from behaving like suggestions.”\\n\\nMurmur. Relief from some. Resentment from the man whose role had just been nudged aside by competence.\\n\\nShe set her angle-cage on the table like a story prop and aligned two cords with the hall’s ribs. “Forces move. We don’t stop them. We redirect. If you want to keep your district from taking pressure meant for the Crown, you do three things: stop leaning on braces when you’re angry, stop hanging laundry on hangers, and stop building your stalls against walls that are named ‘proof.’”\\n\\nLaughter. Not unkind. Laughter bought attention. She spent it.\\n\\nJhace spoke five words, because five from him were worth fifty from most. “We will not perform today.”\\n\\nA ripple of disappointed noise. She held the cord taut over it. “No demonstration. You want to see the work, you come with us to a site and you carry tools. If you want a show, attend a play.”\\n\\nChloen had set their tools on the table like exhibits. She lifted the torque key and turned it in her hands with respect that read in the back row. “This one kills you if you go fast.”\\n\\nBram folded his arms and let that land.\\n\\nQuestions came hot and then cooled. People like the dignity of being told the truth by someone who respects their time. Tiffani gave them the truth as a list:\\n\\n“Costs. His vein is at **0.8** and will not go backward. My hands stiffen and tremor if I overreach. We will say ‘stop’ to each other and mean it. When we say ‘no’ to you, it will be because the work decides, not because we are greedy with competence.”\\n\\nA woman near the back stood. “So you’re together.”\\n\\nThe room did its small quiet the way rooms do when they smell a different show. Tiffani let the silence stand and gave it a use. “We are partners in the work,” she said. “We’ll be where the load needs us.” She left other words unspent.\\n\\nA boy near the front raised a hand without waiting to be seen. “Do you get scared?”\\n\\nJhace considered and did not force the answer to be pretty. “Yes,” he said. “If I don’t, I’m not paying attention.”\\n\\nThe room steadied. The faction man nodded as if he had intended this all along. Tiffani did not correct him. She saved that energy for work.\\n\\nWhen the session ended, the room pushed for a demonstration anyway, because the room was made of people. Tiffani stood her ground. “No.” Jhace said it with her. Two voices. One answer. The hall accepted the denial and turned it into respect.\\n\\n**// SLOT A — End Debrief (short)**\\n\\nThey closed the door behind the last hand and leaned, because people are a load. “Public claim,” Tiffani said.\\n\\nJhace’s mouth didn’t move, but his eyes did. “No,” he said again, quieter. It had other meanings now. She heard them and filed them under Future.\\n\\n**<!--Montage swapped for live interaction; Dynamics: Tiffani–Jhace public claim (unity), Tiffani–Bram reliance; Costs: political, not bodily; Slot A short debrief toggles unity; Saga tease: pamphlet mutters of “endings west” stay ambient-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Chapter 10: Under Load — (Jhace POV)\\n\\nPlanning wanted to be clean. The city wanted to be messy. They met in the yard and negotiated.\\n\\n“Sites,” Bram said, tapping the chalk map. “Two today if we’re lucky. One if the world remembers who it is.”\\n\\nTiffani traced the line of risers with a finger she pretended didn’t ache. “This span first. Cross-lines are close. If we pre-shape here, we buy the wall margin at the turn.”\\n\\n“Sequence,” Jhace said, and they built the day.\\n\\nThe tremor was constant now, a fine thread he wrapped his grip around and used. He logged it—because that’s what you do when a flaw becomes part of the tool.\\n\\n“Chloen,” he said, “you’re lead on gauges today.”\\n\\nHer eyes widened and then narrowed the way a person decides to be equal to a thing. “I’ll get it right.”\\n\\n“You’ll get it honest,” he corrected. “Right follows.”\\n\\nThey stepped off the yard and into the street and the street decided to be a crowd again. Not a hostile one. An interested one. Attention is a kind of pressure. It flexed around them until breathing felt like work.\\n\\n“Slot,” Bram murmured. “You smell it?”\\n\\n“I do,” Jhace said. He did not like preambles. He liked preparations. He felt for Tiffani and found her shoulder where it would be if you had built a person and asked them to stand like a brace.\\n\\nThey paused in the shadow of a proof rib. The crowd swelled a pace ahead and then held a respectful line because they’d been taught yesterday.\\n\\n**// SLOT C — Vulnerability confession (crowd fear)\\n\\nJhace said, without looking at her, “I can’t carry all of this.”\\n\\nTiffani’s breath checked. He had never used first-person like that about the work. He always hid in metal and plural.\\n\\nHe kept his eyes on the rib. “My hand shakes. My sight narrows when the third note gets close. I smell copper when I shouldn’t. If I push past it for the sake of a show, I will break something you can’t hold for me.”\\n\\nShe didn’t touch him. She aligned herself with him. “I know,” she said. “I don’t want a show. I want you upright at the end of the day.”\\n\\nHe let the words hit and sink through. The crowd’s murmur became a sea-noise beyond the rib. “I don’t know how to not be the person who takes the wheel when it needs taking.”\\n\\n“Then be the person who calls the sequence,” she said. “It’s the same courage with a different grip.”\\n\\nHe breathed once. Twice. The third time, his jaw unlocked. He nodded a fraction. “Hold me to it.”\\n\\n“I will,” she said, and the promise cost her hands. He respected the cost more than the comfort.\\n\\nThey stepped out. The crowd folded back around work, not spectacle.\\n\\n**// end SLOT C**\\n\\nAt the first span, the riser sang high. Chloen called it steady. Jhace placed a clamp and didn’t take the wheel. He pointed. Bram pulled. Tiffani set her palms and called two holds in a register just below human hearing. The tremor threaded the whole operation and nothing fell.\\n\\nBy last light, they had one site done and one honest refusal. Jhace said “No” where he would have said “Yes” last week. The wall lived because of it.\\n\\nAt the day’s end, in the yard’s quiet, Tiffani brushed his sleeve with the back of her hand—**~~accident~~** **not accident;** a touch that said the thing neither of them would name yet.\\n\\nChloen watched everything and pretended to see nothing. Bram packed tools like a man who believed in tomorrow.\\n\\n**<!--Montage replaced: planning + Slot C vulnerability confession; Dynamics: Jhace–Tiffani linger freeze, honesty impressed; Jhace–Chloen honesty standard; Costs: tremor constant; Tease: pre-god whisper plans ambient-->**\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Phase 2 Mini Audit (Ch6–Ch10)\\n\\n| Ch | Beats Hit | Dynamics (1/scene) | Slots Used | Costs/Tease | Notes |\\n|----|-----------|---------------------|------------|-------------|------|\\n| 6 | Teaching sync; mutual learn | Tiffani–Jhace warmth via shared cadence; Tiffani–Chloen authorship share | — | Tiffani stiffness/tremor incipient | Rhythm established; clause variety preserved |\\n| 7 | 2-site set → crowd test | Jhace–Tiffani anticipation/trust; Jhace–Chloen inclusion demand | **Slot C (crowd fear variant)** | Vein **0.5**; pact demonstrated publicly | Montage trimmed; market scene replaces drag |\\n| 8 | Public demo; nausea fight | Jhace–Tiffani conflict-under-care; Bram caution pride | **Slot A (debrief)** | Vein **0.8**; hallucination light | Clear “No performance” rule set |\\n| 9 | Faction wedge; defense | Tiffani–Jhace public claim (unity); Tiffani–Bram reliance | **Slot A (short)** | Political cost | Room respects denial; no show given |\\n| 10 | Work choice; brush | Jhace–Tiffani vulnerability confession; Chloen honesty impressed | **Slot C (vulnerability)** | Tremor constant | Ends with motion; refusal earns wall life |\\n\"}"
